range bindingSubjects {\n\t\tif appliesToUser(user, bindingSubject, namespace) {\n\t\t\treturn i, true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn 0, false\n}\n\nfunc has(set []string, ele string) bool {\n\tfor _, s := range set {\n\t\tif s == ele {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\nfunc appliesToUser(user user.Info, subject rbacv1.Subject, namespace string) bool {\n\tswitch subject.Kind {\n\tcase rbacv1.UserKind:\n\t\treturn user.GetName() == subject.Name\n\n\tcase rbacv1.GroupKind:\n\t\treturn has(user.GetGroups(), subject.Name)\n\n\tcase rbacv1.ServiceAccountKind:\n\t\t// default the namespace to namespace we're working in if its available.  This allows rolebindings that reference\n\t\t// SAs in th local namespace to avoid having to qualify them.\n\t\tsaNamespace := namespace\n\t\tif len(subject.Namespace) > 0 {\n\t\t\tsaNamespace = subject.Namespace\n\t\t}\n\t\tif len(saNamespace) == 0 {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t\t// use a more efficient comparison for RBAC checking\n\t\treturn serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(saNamespace, subject.Name, user.GetName())\n\tdefault:\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n}\n\n// NewTestRuleResolver returns a rule resolver from lists of role objects.\nfunc NewTestRuleResolver(roles []*rbacv1.Role, roleBindings []*rbacv1.RoleBinding, clusterRoles []*rbacv1.ClusterRole, clusterRoleBindings []*rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding) (AuthorizationRuleResolver, *StaticRoles) {\n\tr := StaticRoles{\n\t\troles: newMockRuleResolver(r *StaticRoles) AuthorizationRuleResolver {\n\treturn NewDefaultRuleResolver(r, r, r, r)\n}\n\n// StaticRoles is a rule resolver that resolves from lists of role objects.\ntype StaticRoles struct {\n\troles               []*rbacv1.Role\n\troleBindings        []*rbacv1.RoleBinding\n\tclusterRoles        []*rbacv1.ClusterRole\n\tclusterRoleBindings []*rbacv1.ClusterRoleBinding\n}\n\nfunc (r *StaticRoles) GetRole(ctx context.Context, namespace, name string) (*rbacv1.Role, error) {\n\tif len(namespace) == 0 {\n\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"must provide namespace when getting role\")\n\t}\n\tfor _, role := range r.roles {\n\t\tif role.Namespace == namespace && role.Name == name {\n\t\t\treturn role, nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil, errors.New(\"role not found\")\n}\n\nfunc (r *StaticRoles) GetClusterRole(ctx context.Context, name string) (*rbacv1.ClusterRole, error) {\n\tfor _, clusterRole := range r.clusterRoles {\n\t\tif clusterRole.Name == name {\n\t\t\treturn clusterRole, nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil, errors.New(\"clusterrole not found\")\n}\n\nfunc (r *StaticRoles) ListRoleBindings(ctx context.Context, namespace packages in kubernetes/kubernetes. The core authorization logic is in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/, while the REST API handlers and policy enforcement are in pkg/registry/.\\n\\n## Core RBAC Authorizer\\nThe RBACAuthorizer struct (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go) implements the Authorize method which evaluates authorization requests by checking if a user's rules (obtained from RoleBindings and ClusterRoleBindings) allow the requested action. The RequestToRuleMapper interface defines how rules are retrieved for a user.\\n\\n## Subject Access Evaluation\\nSubjectAccessEvaluator (plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go) implements the SubjectLocator interface to determine which subjects (users, groups, service accounts) can perform a given action. It evaluates both cluster-wide and namespaced bindings.\\n\\n## Rule Resolution\\nDefaultRuleResolver (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go) resolves PolicyRules for a user by examining RoleBindings, ClusterRoleBindings, and their referenced Roles and ClusterRoles. The resolver implements the AuthorizationRuleResolver interface with methods RulesFor(), VisitRulesFor(), and GetRoleReferenceRules().\\n\\n## REST Handlers\\nSubjectAccessReview REST handler (pkg/registry/authorization/subjectaccessreview/rest.go) exposes RBAC decisions through an API endpoint, calling the Authorizer.Authorize() method to evaluate access requests. Additional handlers include LocalSubjectAccessReview, SelfSubjectAccessReview, and SelfSubjectRulesReview.\\n\\n## Bootstrap Policies\\nBootstrap RBAC policies are defined in plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/ with three main files:\\n- policy.go: Defines default ClusterRoles and ClusterRoleBindings\\n- namespace_policy.go: Defines default Roles and RoleBindings in reserved kube-* namespaces\\n- controller_policy.go: Defines RBAC for system controllers\\n\\nThese policies are initialized via RESTStorageProvider.PostStartHook() in pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go.\\n\\n## Escalation Prevention\\nPrivilege escalation is prevented through multiple layers:\\n\\n1. EscalationAllowed() (pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go) checks if a user is in system:masters group\\n2. RoleEscalationAuthorized() verifies explicit authorization for the \\\"escalate\\\" verb on roles\\n3. BindingAuthorized() verifies authorization for the \\\"bind\\\" verb before allowing role bindings\\n4. ConfirmNoEscalation() (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go) validates that a user cannot grant permissions they don't have\\n\\n## Policy-Based Storage\\nPolicy-based storage classes enforce escalation prevention:\\n- pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go: Role storage\\n- pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go: ClusterRole storage with aggregation rule support\\n- pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go: RoleBinding storage\\n- pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go: ClusterRoleBinding storage\\n\\nEach storage wrapper's Create() and Update() methods check escalation authorization before allowing modifications. For roles, they verify the rules don't exceed the user's permissions. For ClusterRoles with aggregation rules, they require cluster-admin privileges.\\n\\n## Helper Functions\\nIsOnlyMutatingGCFields() (pkg/registry/rbac/helpers.go) allows GC-related field mutations to bypass escalation checks.
